L3 = R2 = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # R3 = L2 ^ F2 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Round 3 (k5):\n    # F3 = F(R3 ^ k5) = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # L4 = R3 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # R4 = L3 ^ F3 = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cr ^ A = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Subtract: Cl - (Cr ^ A) = (k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3) - (k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3)\n    #                       = F0 ^ F2 ^ k0\n    # Hmm \n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # But F0 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    #      F2 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Choose A = 0 as well (so P = 0):\n    # \n    # L0 = k0\n    # R0 = k0 ^ k1\n    # \n    # Round 0:\n    # F0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # L1 = k0 ^ k1\n    # R1 = k0 ^ F0\n    # \n    # Round 1:\n    # F1 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # L2 = k0 ^ F0\n    # R2 = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # \n    # Round 2:\n    # F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Round 3:\n    # F3 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # Cr = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Cl ^ Cr = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3 ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # Cl ^ Cr = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # F2 depends on A, k0, k1, F1, k4 = k0 ^ k1 ^ F(k0 ^ F0 ^ k3) ^ F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F(k0 ^ F0 ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    # F3 depends on A, k0, F0, F2, k5 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # With P = 0 (A = B = 0):\n    # Cr = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # F0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # F1 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # F3 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # Cr = k0 ^ k1 ^ F(k0 ^ F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ k3) ^ F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # This is a complex equation in k0-k5.\n    # \n    # With just P = 0, we have two equations (Cr, Cl) in 6 unknown keys.\n    # But each key is only 16 bits, so 96 bits total.\n    # We need more plaintexts.\n    # \n    # Let's use P = 0 and P' where A ≠ 0, B = 0.\n    # \n    # For P (A=B=0): Cr = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3, Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # For P' (A=a, B=0): Cr' = a ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1' ^ F3', Cl' = k1 ^ F0' ^ F2' ^ F1' ^ F3'\n    # \n    # Where: F0' = F(a ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    #         F1' = F(a ^ k0 ^ F0' ^ k3)\n    #         F2' = F(a ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1' ^ k4)\n    #         F3' = F(a ^ k0 ^ F0' ^ F2' ^ k5)\n    # \n    # Cr' ^ Cl' ^ a = k0 ^ F0' ^ F2'\n    # \n    # This gives relationships. But solving directly is hard.\n    # \n    # Let me try yet another approach.\n    # \n    # We want k5. We have 2^16 candidates.\n    # For each candidate, we can compute F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5) for any input\n    # IF we know k0, F0, F2.\n    # \n    # Those depend on k0-k4.\n    # \n    # Insight: Choose plaintexts such that F0 & F2 are invariant even if\n    # we don't know k0-k4 exactly.\n    # \n    # Or: realize that we can treat (k0, k1, k2, k3, k4) as a single 80-bit\n    # unknown and just iterate over k5, checking consistency.\n    # \n    # For each k5, we have consistency conditions across plaintexts.\n    # If the conditions are inconsistent (no valid k0-k4 exists), reject k5.\n    # \n    # Here's the key insight for a practical attack:\n    # Use the structure Feistel structure.\n    # \n    # For the last round (round 3):\n    #   F(R3 ^ k5) = R4 ^ L3\n    # \n    # We know R4 = Cr (from ciphertext's right half).\n    # We don't know L3 or R3 directly.\n    # \n    # But: L3 = R2 and R3 = L2 ^ F(R2 ^ k4)\n    #      L2 = R1 and R2 = L1 ^ F(R1 ^ k3)\n    #      L1 = R0 and R1 = L0 ^ F(R0 ^ k2)\n    # \n    # Going backward through the Feistel rounds...\n    # \n    # Let's trace the encryption carefully for arbitrary plaintext P = (A, B).\n    # \n    # After whitening: (L0, R0) = (A ^ k0, B ^ k1)\n    # After pre-mix: (L0, R0) = (A ^ k0, B ^ k1 ^ A ^ k0) = (A ^ k0, A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1)\n    # \n    # Round 0 (key k2): F0 = F(R0 ^ k2), (L1, R1) = (R0, L0 ^ F0)\n    # Round 1 (key k3): F1 = F(R1 ^ k3), (L2, R2) = (R1, L1 ^ F1)\n    # Round 2 (key k4): F2 = F(R2 ^ k4), (L3, R3) = (R2, L2 ^ F2)\n    # Round 3 (key k5): F3 = F(R3 ^ k5), (L4, R4) = (R3, L3 ^ F3)\n    # \n    # Final: L4 ^= R4, output = (R4, L4)\n    # \n    # Let me compute intermediate values:\n    # \n    # Round 0:\n    # F0 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # L1 = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1\n    # R1 = A ^ k0 ^ F0\n    # \n    # Round 1:\n    # F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # L2 = A ^ k0 ^ F0\n    # R2 = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # \n    # Round 2:\n    # F2 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # L3 = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # R3 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Round 3 (k5):\n    # F3 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # L4 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # R4 = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Final XOR: L4 ^= R4\n    # L4_final = L4 ^ R4 = (A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2) ^ (A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3)\n    #          = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # ciphertext = (R4, L4_final) = (Cr, Cl)\n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # OK now let's verify: Cr ^ Cl = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 ^ B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    #                        = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2  ✓\n    # \n    # Now we have a simpler form:\n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cr ^ Cl = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Where: F0 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    #         F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    #         F2 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    #         F3 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # We want to find k5. F3 depends on k5.\n    # \n    # The other terms (F0, F1, F2) don't depend on k5.\n    # \n    # Strategy: use multiple plaintexts to first solve for k0-k4,\n    # then compute k5.\n    # \n    # But here's a simpler differential approach:\n    # \n    # For a given plaintext P = (A, B), define:\n    #   X = R3 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    #   Y = F(X ^ k5) = F3\n    # \n    # From the equations:\n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ Y\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ Y\n    # \n    # Cl ^ Cr = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2  (doesn't depend on Y or k5)\n    # \n    # Adding them (in terms of reconstruction):\n    # Cr ^ Cl = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # For the correct k0, k1, k2, k3, k4, this holds.\n    # \n    # For finding k5, note that:\n    # Y = F(X ^ k5)\n    # \n    # X ^ Y = (A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2) ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # Hmm this doesn't simplify to something directly solvable.\n    # \n    # Let me try this instead:\n    # \n    # From Cr and Cl, we can isolate F3 (which is F(X ^ k5)):\n    # \n    # Cr ^ A ^ B = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # (Cr ^ A ^ B) ^ Cl = (k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3) ^ (B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3)\n    #                    = Cr ^ A ^ B ^ Cl = k0 ^ B ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Not helpful directly.\n    # \n    # Try: Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Hmm, we still have F0 and F2.\n    # \n    # Let me try to eliminate F1 and F3:\n    # \n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3  ... (1)\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3  ... (2)\n    # \n    # (1) ^ (2): Cr ^ Cl = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2  ... (3)\n    # \n    # From (1): F1 ^ F3 = Cr ^ A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1  ... (4)\n    # From (2): F1 ^ F3 = Cl ^ B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2  ... (5)\n    # \n    # From (4) and (5): Cr ^ A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 = Cl ^ B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    #                 Cr ^ A ^ k0 = Cl ^ F0 ^ F2\n    #                 Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2  ... same as (3)\n    # \n    # OK so we really have two independent pieces of info per plaintext:\n    # 1. Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # 2. Cr ^ A ^ B = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Where F0, F1, F2, F3 are as defined.\n    # \n    # The first equation doesn't involve k5!\n    # The second equation involves F3 which involves k5.\n    # \n    # Strategy: Use multiple plaintexts to solve for k0-k4 first\n    # using the first equation. Then use the second equation to find k5.\n    # \n    # For simplicity in solving, let's choose B = A for plaintexts.\n    # \n    # With B = A: F0 = F(k2), F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3), F2 = F(A ^ k3 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Well F0 = F(A ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) which is constant!\n    # \n    # This is promising. If we choose B = A, then F0 is constant (doesn't depend on A).\n    # \n    # With B = A:\n    # F0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) = constant K0\n    # F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ k3)\n    # F2 = F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ F1 ^ k4)  (wait, that's wrong)\n    # \n    # Let me redo:\n    # With B = A:\n    # F0 = F(A ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) = K0 (constant)\n    # \n    # For F1: F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3) = F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ k3)\n    # \n    # For F2: F2 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    #          = F(A ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    #          = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # So F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Cr = A ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = A ^ k1 ^ K0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl = k0 ^ K0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Since K0 is constant, and F2 is a function of F1, and F1 is a function of A,\n    # Cr ^ Cl = k0 ^ K0 ^ F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    # \n    # This is a function of A. By varying A (with B = A), we get different equations.\n    # \n    # Importantly, K0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) is constant, and k5 doesn't appear in Cr ^ Cl!\n    # \n    # So with multiple (A, A) plaintexts, we can solve for k0, k1, k2, k3, k4.\n    # \n    # Once we know k0-k4, we can recover k5 from the Cr equation:\n    # F3 = Cr ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # F3 = F(R3 ^ k5) where R3 = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # So: F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ F2 ^ k5) = Cr ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # \n    # With known k0-k4, we can compute all these except k5.\n    # We need to find x such that F(x) = known_value, where x = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5.\n    # Then k5 = x ^ A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2.\n    # \n    # Since F is not easily invertible, we loop through k5 candidates.\n    # \n    # For each k5 in our 2^16 candidates:\n    #   Check if F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5) == Cr ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # The one that matches is the correct k5.\n    # \n    # So overall:\n    # 1. Choose multiple plaintexts (A, A) and collect Cr, Cl.\n    # 2. Solve for k0-k4 using the relation Cr ^ Cl = A ^ k0 ^ F0... wait, we derived Cr ^ Cl = k0 ^ K0 ^ F2 with B=A.\n    # \n    # Actually let me recompute Cr ^ Cl with B = A:\n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 = A ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3 = A ^ k1 ^ K0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 ^ A ^ k1 ^ K0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    #         = A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # So: Cr ^ Cl = A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ F2\n    # And F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ K0 ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    # \n    # For this to be useful, we need K0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2).\n    # \n    # Hmm, k0 and K0 and k4 are entangled here. This is complex.\n    # \n    # Let me try a different plaintext structure: B = 0.\n    # \n    # With B = 0:\n    # F0 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)... wait that's wrong\n    # \n    # F2 = F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4) = F(A ^ 0 ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4) = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Cr = A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = B ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3 = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl = A ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # OK this is cleaner. Cr ^ Cl = A ^ F0 ^ F2, independent of k5.\n    # \n    # F0 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # F2 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # \n    # By picking A values (with B = 0), we can solve for k0, k1, k2, k3, k4.\n    # \n    # Let's denote: \n    # - A_i is the i-th A value we choose\n    # - Cr_i, Cl_i are the corresponding ciphertext halves\n    # \n    # For each i: Cr_i ^ Cl_i ^ A_i = F0(A_i) ^ F2(A_i)\n    #          = F(A_i ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ F(A_i ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1(A_i) ^ k4)\n    # \n    # where F1(A_i) = F(A_i ^ k0 ^ F0(A_i) ^ k3).\n    # \n    # We have 5 unknowns (k0-k4), each from a 16-bit seed.\n    # With enough A values, we can solve for these.\n    # \n    # Actually, this is still complex. Let me think of a more practical approach.\n    # \n    # PRACTICAL APPROACH:\n    # Since k5 has only 2^16 possibilities, and we're asked to recover k5,\n    # let's just test all 2^16 candidates directly.\n    # \n    # For a well-chosen plaintext, the correct k5 will give the expected output.\n    # But we don't have a way to compute the expected output without knowing k0-k4.\n    # \n    # ALTERNATIVE: Use a differential relation that cancels out k0-k4.\n    # \n    # Consider two plaintexts P1 = (A, 0) and P2 = (A', 0) with the same B = 0.\n    # \n    # For P1: Cr1 = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1_1 ^ F3_1, Cl1 = k0 ^ F0_1 ^ F2_1\n    #        where (Cr1 ^ Cl1 ^ A = k0 ^ F0_1 ^ F2_1... no wait)\n    # \n    # Cr1 ^ Cl1 = A ^ F0_1 ^ F2_1\n    # Cr2 ^ Cl2 = A' ^ F0_2 ^ F2_2\n    # \n    # The difference: (Cr1 ^ Cl1) ^ (Cr2 ^ Cl2 ^ A ^ A') = F0_1 ^ F2_1 ^ F0_2 ^ F2_2\n    # \n    # This helps relate the keys.\n    # \n    # Actually, here's a clever observation:\n    # \n    # Cr = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # Cl ^ Cr = A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # So: F3 = Cr ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    #      F3 = Cl ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1\n    # \n    # Equating the two expressions for F3:\n    # Cr ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 = Cl ^ k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1\n    # Cr ^ A ^ k0 = Cl ^ F0 ^ F2\n    # \n    # Which is the same as Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2. Good.\n    # \n    # Now, F3 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # And F3 = Cr ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # \n    # So: F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5) = Cr ^ A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1\n    # \n    # For a single plaintext, this is one equation relating k5 and the other keys.\n    # For multiple plaintexts, we get multiple equations.\n    # \n    # The key insight is: F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5) is computable for each k5 candidate,\n    # IF we know k0, F0, F2, k1, F1, Cr, A.\n    # \n    # We know Cr and A (we choose A).\n    # We don't know k0, k1, F0, F1, F2.\n    # \n    # But those depend on k0-k4 and our chosen A.\n    # \n    # Here's a simpler approach: brute force k0-k4 for a specific k5 candidate.\n    # \n    # For each k5 in 2^16 candidates:\n    #   For each tuple (k0,k1,k2,k3,k4) in 2^80 possibilities (too many!)\n    #     Check consistency against multiple plaintexts.\n    # \n    # This is too slow.\n    # \n    # BETTER: Solve for k0-k4 first (without k5), then find k5.\n    # \n    # The equation Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 doesn't involve k5.\n    # \n    # For B = 0 plaintexts:\n    # F0 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    # F1 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    # F2 = F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # Cr ^ Cl ^ A = k0 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    # \n    # This is a complex function of k0-k4, but for each A it gives a 32-bit value.\n    # \n    # With enough A values, we can solve for k0-k4.\n    # Actually, each key is from a 16-bit seed, so only 2^16 possibilities per key.\n    # \n    # Brute force a single key at a time:\n    # 1. Try all 2^16 values of k0. For each, check consistency across plaintexts.\n    # 2. With k0 fixed, try all 2^16 values of k1. Repeat.\n    # 3. Continue for k2, k3, k4.\n    # 4. Finally, find k5.\n    # \n    # This gives 5 * 2^16 * (# plaintexts) operations.\n    # With # plaintexts = 4 or so, this is about 2^20 operations, very fast!\n    # \n    # Let me implement this.\n    # \n    # FIXING APPROACH:\n    # Try all 2^16 values for k0 first. For each, compute expected values\n    # of Cr ^ Cl ^ A for various A (with B = 0). See which k0 candidates\n    # are consistent.\n    # \n    # Hmm wait, Cr ^ Cl ^ A depends on all of k0-k4. We need to solve\n    # jointly.\n    # \n    # OK let me just try a different, more direct strategy.\n    # \n    # Given the complexity of the key schedule relationships,\n    # and the fact that k5 has only 2^16 possible values,\n    # let's use a probabilistic approach.\n    # \n    # For several chosen plaintexts, for each k5 candidate,\n    # check if there exists some (k0,...,k4) that's consistent.\n    # The correct k5 should pass all checks, while random k5 will fail.\n    # \n    # Hmm but checking existence is hard.\n    # \n    # FINAL STRATEGY (that will work):\n    # \n    # 1. The keys are derived: key[i] = (seed[i] * 1234567) & 0xFFFFFFFF\n    # 2. Each seed[i] is 16 bits.\n    # 3. We'll search for k5 by testing all 2^16 candidates.\n    # 4. For each k5 candidate, test consistency.\n    # \n    # For constraint checking, use this observation:\n    # \n    # For plaintexts P and P' where only the left half differs (A != A', but same B=0):\n    # \n    # We have Cr = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3 and Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # The term F3 = F(A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5) depends on A and k5.\n    # \n    # If we use A and A' such that A ^ k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 is the same for both,\n    # then F3 would be the same for both, and the difference Cr ^ Cr'\n    # would be just A ^ A'.\n    # \n    # But actually F0, F1, F2 depend on A in complex ways.\n    # \n    # Let me try a more practical differential approach:\n    # \n    # Choose plaintexts where B = 0 and A varies widely.\n    # For A = 0:\n    #   F0 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ k2)\n    #   F1 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ k3)\n    #   F2 = F(k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ k4)\n    #   F3 = F(k0 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ k5)\n    #   Cr = k0 ^ k1 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    #   Cl = k1 ^ F0 ^ F2 ^ F1 ^ F3\n    # \n    # This is for A=0, B=0. We have access to the encrypt_fn which uses ALL keys.\n    # So we can encrypt any plaintext and get the ciphertext.\n    #\n    # Here's the key: we can use the internal structure of the encryption\n    # to deduce k5.\n    #\n    # The round 3 computation is: F(right ^ k5)\n    #\n    # If we can make right (before round 3) take a known value,\n    # we can compute F(known_value ^ k5) and then recover k5.\n    #\n    # Right before round 3 is: R3 = L2 ^ F(R2 ^ k4)\n    # R2 before round 2, etc.\n    #\n    # Let me trace back from plaintext to R3:\n    #\n    # With P = (A, B):\n    # After whitening: (L, R) = (A ^ k0, B ^ k1)\n    # After pre-mix: (L, R) = (A ^ k0, B ^ k1 ^ A ^ k0) = (A ^ k0, A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1)\n    #\n    # Round 0: (L, R) = (A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1, A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2))\n    # Round 1: (L, R) = (A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2), A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ F(...) ^ k3))\n    # Round 2: (L, R) = (A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(...), A ^ k0 ^ F(...) ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(...) ^ k4))\n    #\n    # So R3 = A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ B ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ k3) ^ k4)\n    #\n    # This is a complex function of A, B, and keys 0-4.\n    #\n    # PRACTICAL SOLUTION:\n    #\n    # Since all this analysis is getting complex, let me implement a simpler approach.\n    #\n    # We'll use multiple plaintexts to narrow down k5.\n    # For each k5 candidate, we'll compute a score based on how well it\n    # explains the ciphertexts.\n    #\n    # The score for a k5 candidate is:\n    # For each plaintext, check if Cr ^ 1 ^ A computed from k5 is consistent.\n    # \n    # Actually, let me just do this: since k5 has only 2^16 values,\n    # and we have the encrypt_fn, let me think of how to use it.\n    #\n    # We CAN query encrypt_fn with ANY plaintext.\n    #\n    # What if we do this:\n    # 1. Encrypt P1 = (A1, B1), get C1.\n    # 2. For each k5 candidate, simulate round 3: compute F(R3_candidate ^ k5)\n    #    where R3_candidate is computed assuming we can deduce R3 from C1.\n    # \n    # From C1, we know Cr1 and Cl1.\n    # Cr1 = R4 = L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    # Cl1 = L4_final = R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #\n    # Solving: Let X = F(R3 ^ k5).\n    # Cr1 = L3 ^ X  ... (1)\n    # Cl1 = R3 ^ L3 ^ X  ... (2)\n    #\n    # (1) ^ (2): Cr1 ^ Cl1 = L3 ^ X ^ R3 ^ L3 ^ X = R3\n    # So R3 = Cr1 ^ Cl1!\n    #\n    # Yes! We can compute R3 directly from the ciphertext!\n    #\n    # Then: X = F(R3 ^ k5) = Cr1 ^ L3 = Cr1 ^ R2 (since L3 = R2)\n    # But we don't know R2 directly.\n    #\n    # Wait, let me re-examine the round structure.\n    #\n    # Round 3:\n    #   mixed = F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #   temp = R3\n    #   right = L3 ^ mixed = L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #   left = R3\n    #\n    # After round 3: (L4, R4) = (R3, L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5))\n    #\n    # Post-round mixing: L4 ^= R4, so L4_final = R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #\n    # Final swap: ciphertext = merge(R4, L4_final)\n    #                     = merge(L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5), R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5))\n    #\n    # So Cr = L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #    Cl = R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #\n    # Cr ^ Cl = (L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)) ^ (R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5))\n    #         = R3\n    #\n    # So R3 = Cr ^ Cl (computable from ciphertext!)\n    #\n    # Then: F(R3 ^ k5) = Cr ^ L3 = Cr ^ R2 (since L3 = R2)\n    #\n    # Hmm, we still need R2 (which is L3). Let me think...\n    #\n    # We have: Cl = R3 ^ L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    # We know Cl and R3. Let Y = F(R3 ^ k5). Then:\n    # Cl = R3 ^ L3 ^ Y\n    # L3 = R3 ^ Cl ^ Y\n    #\n    # But Y = F(R3 ^ k5), so:\n    # L3 = R3 ^ Cl ^ F(R3 ^ k5)\n    #\n    # Also: Cr = L3 ^ F(R3 ^ k5) = (R3 ^ Cl ^ F(R3 ^ k5)) ^ F(R3 ^ k5) = R3 ^ Cl\n    # Wait, that gives R3 = Cr ^ Cl, which matches.\n    #\n    # But we can't directly solve for k5 from here alone.\n    # We have: F(R3 ^ k5) = Cr ^ L3\n    # And L3 = R3 ^ Cl ^ F(R3 ^ k5) = R3 ^ Cl ^ Cr ^ L3\n    # This seems circular.\n    #\n    # Let me approach differently. Since R3 = Cr ^ Cl, this is Cl = Cr ^ Cl ^ Cr = Cl, an identity.\n    #\n    # So we can't distinguish k5 candidates from a single ciphertext.\n    #\n    # But we can use the fact that L3 must equal R2 from round 2.\n    # For each plaintext P, we compute R3 = Cr ^ Cl.\n    # For each k5 candidate, we compute F(R3 ^ k5).\n    #\n    # For the correct k5, the values F(R3 ^ k5) should be consistent\n    # with the rest of the encryption (i.e., there exist valid k0-k4).\n    #\n    #     # Simple heuristic: the correct k5 should give \"nice\" L3 values.\n    # \"Nice\" means L3 should be roughly the same as A XOR some constant.\n    # \n    # L3 = A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ F(A ^ k0 ^ k1 ^ k2) ^ k3)\n    #\n    # The F term is relatively small (depends on bytes of input).\n    # So L3 ^ A ≈ k0 ^ k1 ^ small value.\n    #\n    # For different A values, L3 ^ A should have the same approximate\n    # value (k0 ^ k1) with small variations.\n    #\n    # Let me implement this check.\n    \n    print(\"Using heuristic check...\")\n    \n    best_k5 = None\n    best_variance = float('inf')\n    \n    for seed in range(65536):\n        k5 = (seed * MULTIPLIER) & 0xFFFFFFFF\n        \n        X = []\n        for i, (cr, cl) in enumerate(ciphertexts):\n            r3 = cr ^ cl\n            h = f(r3 ^ k5)\n            l3 = cr ^ h\n            A = A_vals[i]\n            X.append(l3 ^ A)\n        \n        # Compute variance of X\n        mean = sum(X) // len(X)\n        variance = sum((x - mean) ** 2 for x in X) // len(X)\n        \n        if variance < best_variance:\n            best_variance = variance\n            best_k5 = k5\n    \n    print(f\"Best k5: {best_k5}, variance: {best_variance}\")\n    \n    return best_k5\nEOF\n","duration":1.0}]}
